<div id="review_668364919" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/668364919" />
    <a title="Joann" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3254508-joann"><img alt="Joann" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584224255p2/3254508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/668364919?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joann" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joann" href="/user/show/3254508-joann">Joann</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3254508-joann?shelf=challenge">challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3254508-joann?shelf=amazing-cover">amazing-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3254508-joann?shelf=great-couple">great-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3254508-joann?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer668364919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10422111880454775199"><b>Cover:</b><br/>This cover is very pretty. The girl on the front fits Charli quite perfectly, and really is how I pictured her through out the book. The font's are simple and subdued which fits the image wonderfully. Perfect cover for this book!<br/><br/><b>First Reaction:</b><br/>Sometimes it's nice to read a book which just... nice. Simple, easy, no love triangles, no murders, <s>no wizards trying to kidnap some important political figure and take them into the future where they create a devise which could blow up the universe.</s></span>
  <span id="freeText10422111880454775199" style="display:none"><b>Cover:</b><br />This cover is very pretty. The girl on the front fits Charli quite perfectly, and really is how I pictured her through out the book. The font's are simple and subdued which fits the image wonderfully. Perfect cover for this book!<br /><br /><b>First Reaction:</b><br />Sometimes it's nice to read a book which just... nice. Simple, easy, no love triangles, no murders, <s>no wizards trying to kidnap some important political figure and take them into the future where they create a devise which could blow up the universe.</s> Nope, a nice simple read.<br /><br /><b>What I Think About the Book:</b><br />I love the whole concept of fate, love at first sight and soul mates. Sometime it's near impossible to understand why something happens, why someone is instantly connected to another person and why you life turned in the direction it did. This book draws such a wonderful picture of this. Sometimes fate turns your life upside down, but there may be a perfect reason why.<br /><br />"My head is very protective of my heart and it's a defect I'm well aware of"<br /><br />The setting of this story in Tasmania is such a perfect location. Who wouldn't want to read about sun kissed surfers, sandy shores, old worn sailboats and picturesque rocky coast lines. This is exactly the perfect location for a love to blossom between two people. I personally love the idea of Australia as the setting of a love/coming of age tale. I don't understand why Charli would want o leave such a beautiful place in the first place, maybe it's just a right of passage, the need to extend ones self.<br /><br />I have to say I am usually a much bigger fan of books where the male is more dominate and flaky, not the female in the relationship. I usually like the jerk, or bad boy if you may, but i this story it's not that way at all. Adam is sweet and loving and tries so hard to gain Charli's affection, not my normal cup of tea, but still a great relationship.<br /><br /><b>Final Thoughts:</b><br />A beautiful love/coming of age story, set in a romantic sea side town. Picturesque scenery, budding romance and a sprinkle of witty humor made this story a delight to read. <br /><br />I received this E-Book for free from NetGalley for an honest review. Thank you for the opportunity to read this wonderful book.<br /><br />You can also see this review on my blog <a href="http://thepaperbacklass.blogspot.com/2013/07/review-saving-wishes-by-gj-walker-smith.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Paperback Lass</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1262369492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13010377827899118418">Charlotte Blake lives in a small town called Piper’s Cove with her older brother Alex who has looked after her from a very young age after their mother passed away. She hopes to finally fulfill her dream and leave Piper’s Cove as soon as she graduates from high school and travel the world. The only people who will make it difficult to leave behind her home are her brother and best friend. <br/>Cue in a handsome American boy named Adam Decarie who lives in New York and is visiting his cousin Gabrielle</span>
  <span id="freeText13010377827899118418" style="display:none">Charlotte Blake lives in a small town called Piper’s Cove with her older brother Alex who has looked after her from a very young age after their mother passed away. She hopes to finally fulfill her dream and leave Piper’s Cove as soon as she graduates from high school and travel the world. The only people who will make it difficult to leave behind her home are her brother and best friend. <br />Cue in a handsome American boy named Adam Decarie who lives in New York and is visiting his cousin Gabrielle, who just happens to be the annoying and exasperating French teacher who makes Charli’s high school existence even more intolerable. Their unexpected encounter will change both of their lives. As they begin to spend time together Charli only realizes how much Adam is affecting her emotionally she is struggling to overcome the connection and draw she feels towards him. She doesn’t want to let her guard down and ultimately suffer heartbreak at the hands of gorgeous stranger who will leave in a matter of months. <br />The reluctance Charli has towards allowing her true personality to shine through is because she knows deep down that this stranger will somehow play an integral part in her life.<br />These characters were easily relatable as it made it easier for the reader to make connections with how deep their emotions are affecting them. Each of their personalities shined through specially Charli’s with all the drama surrounding her. <br />There are absolutely no words to describe how much I truly enjoyed reading this beautiful story. I can’t wait to find out what will happen in the installment I highly recommend this book!!!<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15227565546489332414">I loved the story line because it tells the story of an almost broken girl and a boy who tries to get her to see her for who she is. I felt that the setting helped explained some of the characters and their actions, thought, and feelings. I loved how the author set up the book and felt that the author did a pretty good job in introducing all the twisting and turning that went on in the book. In some parts of the book I felt that I was disconnected with the characters, but that was one of the onl</span>
  <span id="freeText15227565546489332414" style="display:none">I loved the story line because it tells the story of an almost broken girl and a boy who tries to get her to see her for who she is. I felt that the setting helped explained some of the characters and their actions, thought, and feelings. I loved how the author set up the book and felt that the author did a pretty good job in introducing all the twisting and turning that went on in the book. In some parts of the book I felt that I was disconnected with the characters, but that was one of the only problems.<br /><br />Charli Blake was an interesting character to say the least. Her reactions and decisions continued to surprise me and I liked that about her character. The author wrote her with a strong personality that anyone can connect with and appreciate. I liked that she didn’t always make the right choices and wasn’t the perfect lead character that always did things right.<br /><br />Adam was an character that really changed Charli’s opinions. I liked how his presence affected Charli and how she responded to him and the many situations they were put in. I felt that sometimes Charli wanted to go way to fast for a guy she just met, but luckily Adam managed to slow her down most of the time. <br /><br />Overall the book was a pretty good read and I look forward to the next book in the series. I will be reading more books by this author and publisher in the nearby future.<br /><br />***I received this book as an eARC for my honest review and opinion.***<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanya" href="/user/show/2051042-tanya">Tanya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2051042-tanya?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer662285038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8683797676285846504">I received this book as an ARC from netgalley...<br/><br/>Wow, it's been a long time since I've pulled an all-nighter because I couldn't put the book down. But this is one of those books for me. The story is about a 17 yr. old named Charli (Charlotte), living in a small town, Pipers Cove off the coast of Tasmania and the relationship she has with Adam, a French-American boy (of whom happens to be her French teacher's cousin) from New York, visiting for his summer break. What I liked about the book was tha</span>
  <span id="freeText8683797676285846504" style="display:none">I received this book as an ARC from netgalley...<br /><br />Wow, it's been a long time since I've pulled an all-nighter because I couldn't put the book down. But this is one of those books for me. The story is about a 17 yr. old named Charli (Charlotte), living in a small town, Pipers Cove off the coast of Tasmania and the relationship she has with Adam, a French-American boy (of whom happens to be her French teacher's cousin) from New York, visiting for his summer break. What I liked about the book was that the dialogue felt real and not forced. The chemistry between the two is instantaneous but it doesn't feel rushed. The characters grow over the course of the book as does their relationship. And for those that are put off by the explicit scenes in romance novels, this is the book for you- It's pretty vanilla with some sprinkles...You still get all of the sparks and don't even miss the chocolate syrup.<br /><br />I heard myself laugh out loud, I was rooting for the relationship to work, I kept wanting to know what was going to happen next because the writing is that good, making me curious about these people (albeit fictitious). And the supporting cast is fleshed out and interesting...<br /><br />I can't wait to read the second in the series, and hope the third comes out soon. Recommend for anyone who wants to read an awesome love story. :0)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8683797676285846504" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8112042490593240944" style="display:none"> I was looking around on my phone to find books I may be interested in and I came across this one. I read this book in one day. It is hands down a book that will keep you smiling throughout. It does have its scenes where your heart may melt or when you feel like you're in the situation and your own heart is breaking. This romantic novel is one of the best books I have ever read. Since reading it and finishing I have downloaded the rest of the sequel and waiting for the newest one to make it's way out. The way the author writes and illustrates everything in the novel makes you feel like as though you're standing there watching everything happen before you. This isn't a romance book that is too sappy it is just filled with love and happiness yet illustrates how consuming love can be at the same time.<br /> I recommend this book 100%. If you like to read books that tend to put a smile on your face and just keep you happy this is a great book! You won't be able to put it down. Since finishing the book I have re-read it also. <br /></span>

<div id="review_687494290" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/687494290" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16808888-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575407777p2/16808888.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/687494290?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/16808888-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer687494290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7077074454782964750"><i>I received this as an ebook for free in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/>Honestly, I really didn't like this book. I read the whole thing, but I barely made it. The whole love at first sight thing? Uhhhhh, no thanks. Charli's goal seemed to be make-it-out-of-this-horrible-town-or-else, and while I did see a bit of growth/change in her character...it felt kinda unnatural. The story was pretty predictable, and the surprises there were felt pretty unnatural. Most of the characters were "cardboard char</span>
  <span id="freeText7077074454782964750" style="display:none"><i>I received this as an ebook for free in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br />Honestly, I really didn't like this book. I read the whole thing, but I barely made it. The whole love at first sight thing? Uhhhhh, no thanks. Charli's goal seemed to be make-it-out-of-this-horrible-town-or-else, and while I did see a bit of growth/change in her character...it felt kinda unnatural. The story was pretty predictable, and the surprises there were felt pretty unnatural. Most of the characters were "cardboard characters," which I really, really hate. I'll forgive a plot that's on the boring side, but only if the characters make up for it. And, well, they didn't. <br /><br />It wasn't the worst book on the planet, but certainly wasn't the best, either. I won't be reading the other books in the series/trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7077074454782964750" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QXFtucOi5OzvrboC6J8YPeaafx6Ov/NctpQncrbpg33MFhWYSRNoeMK7a6xSzli1s8E2alM7IL2Wh3KMxx+4WQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('5CxzJFELNPFj/f6moH2oZIk1QRdw0fXPJNfZW2LQBwxpSwsF27q4ZU7rLwgaLOjs3G4IY61VJi4ExIylEyY8KA==')})
  }
